Additionally handles IPv6 addresses.\n   313→\n   314→    QUrl.fromUserInput handles something like '::1' as a file URL instead of an\n   315→    IPv6, so we first try to handle it as a valid IPv6, https://codereview.qt-project.org/#/c/93851/ has a better way\n   320→            to solve this?\n   321→    https://github.com/qutebrowser/qutebrowser/issues/109\n   322→\n   323→    Args:\n   324→ url2):\n   476→    \"\"\"Check if url1 and url2 belong to the same website.\n   477→\n   478→    This will use a \"public suffix list\" to determine what a \"top level domain\"\n   479→    is. All further domains are ignored.\n   480→\n   481→    For example example.com and www.example.com are considered the same. but\n   482→    example.co.uk and test.co.uk are not.\n   483→\n   484→    Return:\n   485→        True if the domains are the same, False otherwise.\n   486→    \"\"\"\n   487→    if not url1.isValid():\n   488→        raise InvalidUrlError(url1)\n   489→    if not url2.isValid():\n   490→        raise InvalidUrlError(url2)\n   491→\n   492→    suffix1 = url1.topLevelDomain()\n   493→    suffix2 = url2.topLevelDomain()\n   494→    if suffix1 == '':\n   495→        return url1.host() == url2.host()\n   496→\n   497→    if suffix1 != suffix2:\n   498→        return False\n   499→\n   500→    domain1 = url1.host()[:-len(suffix1)].split('.')[-1]\n   501→    domain2 = url2.host()[:-len(suffix2)].split('.')[-1]\n   502→    return domain1 == domain2\n   503→\n   504→\n   505→def encoded_url(url):\n   506→    \"\"\"Return the fully encoded url as string.\n   507→\n   508→    Args:\n   509→        url: The url to encode as QUrl.\n   510→    \"\"\"\n   511→    return bytes(url.toEncoded()).decode('ascii')\n   512→\n   513→\n   514→class IncDecError(Exception):\n   515→\n   516→    \"\"\"Exception raised by incdec_number on problems.\n   517→\n   518→    Attributes:\n   519→        msg: The error message.\n   520→        url: The QUrl which caused the error.\n   521→    \"\"\"\n   522→\n   523→    def __init__(self, msg, url):\n   524→        super().__init__(msg)\n   525→        self.url = url\n   526→        self.msg = msg\n   527→\n   528→    def __str__(self):\n   529→        return '{}: {}'.format(self.msg, self.url.toString())\n   530→\n   531→\n   532→def _get_incdec_value(match, incdec, url, count):\n   533→    \"\"\"Get an incremented/decremented URL based on a URL match.\"\"\"\n   534→    pre, zeroes, number, post = match.groups()\n   535→    # This should always succeed because we match \\d+\n   536→    val = int(number)\n   537→    if incdec == 'decrement':\n   538→        if val <= 0:\n   539→            raise IncDecError(\"Can't decrement {}!\".format(val), url)\n   540→        val -= count\n   541→    elif incdec == 'increment':\n   542→        val += count\n   543→    else:\n   544→        raise ValueError(\"Invalid value {} for indec!\".format(incdec))\n   545→    if zeroes:\n   546→        if len(number) < len(str(val)):\n   547→            zeroes = zeroes[1:]\n   548→        elif len(number) > len(str(val)):\n   549→            zeroes += '0'\n   550→\n   551→    return ''.join([pre, zeroes, str(val), post])\n   552→\n   553→\n   554→def incdec_number(url, incdec, count=1, segments=None):\n   555→    \"\"\"Find a number in the url and increment or decrement it.\n   556→\n   557→    Args:\n   558→        url: The current url\n   559→        incdec: Either 'increment' or 'decrement'\n   560→        count: The number to increment or decrement by\n   561→        segments: A set of URL segments to search. Valid segments are:\n   562→                  'host', 'port', 'path', 'query', 'anchor'.\n   563→                  Default: {'path', 'query'}\n   564→\n   565→    Return:\n   566→        The new url with the number incremented/decremented.\n   567→\n   568→    Raises IncDecError if the url contains no number.\n   569→    \"\"\"\n   570→    if not url.isValid():\n   571→        raise InvalidUrlError(url)\n   572→\n   573→    if segments is None:\n   574→        segments = {'path', 'query'}\n   575→    valid_segments = {'host', 'port', 'path', 'query', 'anchor'}\n   576→    if segments - valid_segments:\n   577→        extra_elements = segments - valid_segments\n   578→        raise IncDecError(\"Invalid segments: {}\".format(\n   579→            ', '.join(extra_elements)), url)\n   580→\n   581→    # Make a copy of the QUrl so we don't modify the original\n   582→    url = QUrl(url)\n   583→    # Order as they appear in a URL\n   584→    segment_modifiers = [\n   585→        ('host', url.host, url.setHost),\n   586→        ('port', lambda: str(url.port()) if url.port() > 0 else '',\n   587→         lambda x: url.setPort(int(x))),\n   588→        ('path', url.path, url.setPath),\n   589→        ('query', url.query, url.setQuery),\n   590→        ('anchor', url.fragment, url.setFragment),\n   591→    ]\n   592→    # We're searching the last number so we walk the url segments backwards\n   593→    for segment, getter, setter in reversed(segment_modifiers):\n   594→        if segment not in segments:\n   595→            continue\n   596→\n   597→        # Additionally handles IPv6 addresses.\n\n    QUrl.fromUserInput handles something like '::1' as a file URL instead of an\n    IPv6, so we first try to handle it as a valid IPv6, and if that fails we\n url1 and url2 belong to the same website.\n\n    This will use a \"public suffix list\" to determine what a \"top level domain\"\n    is. All further domains are ignored.\n\n    For example example.com and www.example.com are considered the same. but\n    example.co.uk and test.co.uk are not.\n\n    Return:\n        True if the domains are the same, False otherwise.\n    \"\"\"\n    if not url1.isValid():\n        raise InvalidUrlError(url1)\n    if not url2.isValid():\n        raise InvalidUrlError(url2)\n\n    suffix1 = url1.topLevelDomain()\n    suffix2 = url2.topLevelDomain()\n    if suffix1 == '':\n        return url1.host() == url2.host()\n\n    if suffix1 != suffix2:\n        return False\n\n    domain1 = url1.host()[:-len(suffix1)].split('.')[-1]\n    domain2 = url2.host()[:-len(suffix2)].split('.')[-1]\n    return domain1 == domain2\n\n\ndef encoded_url(url):\n    \"\"\"Return the fully encoded url as string.\n\n    Args:\n        url: The url to encode as QUrl.\n    \"\"\"\n    return bytes(url.toEncoded()).decode('ascii')\n\n\nclass IncDecError(Exception):\n\n    \"\"\"Exception raised by incdec_number on problems.\n\n    Attributes:\n        msg: The error message.\n        url: The QUrl which caused the error.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, msg, url):\n        super().__init__(msg)\n        self.url = url\n        self.msg = msg\n\n    def __str__(self):\n        return '{}: {}'.format(self.msg, self.url.toString())\n\n\ndef _get_incdec_value(match, incdec, url, count):\n    \"\"\"Get an incremented/decremented URL based on a URL match.\"\"\"\n    pre, zeroes, number, post = match.groups()\n    # This should always succeed because we match \\d+\n    val = int(number)\n    if incdec == 'decrement':\n        if val <= 0:\n            raise IncDecError(\"Can't decrement {}!\".format(val), url)\n        val -= count\n    elif incdec == 'increment':\n        val += count\n    else:\n        raise ValueError(\"Invalid value {} for indec!\".format(incdec))\n    if zeroes:\n        if len(number) < len(str(val)):\n            zeroes = zeroes[1:]\n        elif len(number) > len(str(val)):\n            zeroes += '0'\n\n    return ''.join([pre, zeroes, str(val), post])\n\n\ndef incdec_number(url, incdec, count=1, segments=None):\n    \"\"\"Find a number in the url and increment or decrement it.\n\n    Args:\n        url: The current url\n        incdec: Either 'increment' or 'decrement'\n        count: The number to increment or decrement by\n        segments: A set of URL segments to search. Valid segments are:\n                  'host', 'port', 'path', 'query', 'anchor'.\n                  Default: {'path', 'query'}\n\n    Return:\n        The new url with the number incremented/decremented.\n\n    Raises IncDecError if the url contains no number.\n    \"\"\"\n    if not url.isValid():\n        raise InvalidUrlError(url)\n\n    if segments is None:\n        segments = {'path', 'query'}\n    valid_segments = {'host', 'port', 'path', 'query', 'anchor'}\n    if segments - valid_segments:\n        extra_elements = segments - valid_segments\n        raise IncDecError(\"Invalid segments: {}\".format(\n            ', '.join(extra_elements)), url)\n\n    # Make a copy of the QUrl so we don't modify the original\n    url = QUrl(url)\n    # Order as they appear in a URL\n    segment_modifiers = [\n        ('host', url.host, url.setHost),\n        ('port', lambda: str(url.port()) if url.port() > 0 else '',\n         lambda x: url.setPort(int(x))),\n        ('path', url.path, url.setPath),\n        ('query', url.query, url.setQuery),\n        ('anchor', url.fragment, url.setFragment),\n    ]\n    # We're searching the last number so we walk the url segments backwards\n    for segment, getter, setter in reversed(segment_modifiers):\n        if segment not in segments:\n            continue\n\n        # Get the last number in a string\n        match = re.fullmatch(r'(.*\\D|^)(0*)(\\d+)(.*)', getter())\n        if not match:\n            continue\n\n        setter(_get_incdec_value(match, incdec, url, count))\n        return url\n\n    raise IncDecError(\"No number found in URL!\", url)\n\n\ndef file_url(path):\n    \"\"\"Return a file:// url (as string) to the given local path.\n\n    Arguments:\n        path: The absolute path to the local file\n    \"\"\"\n    return QUrl.fromLocalFile(path).toString(QUrl.FullyEncoded)\n\n\ndef data_url(mimetype, data):\n    \"\"\"Get a data: QUrl for the given data.\"\"\"\n    b64 = base64.b64encode(data).decode('ascii')\n    url = QUrl('data:{};base64,{}'.format(mimetype, b64))\n    qtutils.ensure_valid(url)\n    return url\n\n\ndef safe_display_string(qurl):\n    \"\"\"Get a IDN-homograph phishing safe form of the given QUrl.\n\n    If we're dealing with a Punycode-encoded URL, this prepends the hostname in\n    its encoded form, to make sure those URLs are distinguishable.\n\n    See https://github.com/qutebrowser/qutebrowser/issues/2547\n    and https://bugreports.qt.io/browse/QTBUG-60365\n    \"\"\"\n    if not qurl.isValid():\n        raise InvalidUrlError(qurl)\n\n    host = qurl.host(QUrl.FullyEncoded)\n    if '..' in host:  # {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01M4MqexjocqfWuuvbskdSDr","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Let me now trace through the code to understand the exact bugs. Let me re-examine the incdec_number function more carefully:\n\nLooking at the code in `/app/qutebrowser/utils/urlutils.py`:\n\n```python\ndef incdec_number(url, incdec, count=1, segments=None):\n    ...\n    segment_modifiers = [\n        ('host', url.host, url.setHost),\n        ('port', lambda: str(url.port()) if url.port() > 0 else '',\n         lambda x: url.setPort(int(x))),\n        ('path', url.path, url.setPath),\n        ('query', url.query, url.setQuery),\n        ('anchor', url.fragment, url.setFragment),\n    ]\n    # We're searching the last number so we walk the url segments backwards\n    for segment, getter, setter in reversed(segment_modifiers):\n        if segment not in segments:\n            continue\n\n        # Get the last number in a string\n        match = re.fullmatch(r'(.*\\D|^)(0*)(\\d+)(.*)', getter())\n        if not match:\n            continue\n\n        setter(_get_incdec_value(match, incdec, url, count))\n        return url\n```\n\nThe issue is that `getter()` returns the raw string from the URL. For example:\n- `url.path()` returns the path as-is, including percent-encoded characters\n- So for `/page%205`, it returns that exact string\n- The regex `(.*\\D|^)(0*)(\\d+)(.*)` would match:\n  - pre: `/page%20`\n  - zeroes: ``\n  - number: `5`\n  - post: ``\n- So the 5 gets incremented to 6, giving `/page%206`\n\nThis is correct! So why is there an issue?\n\nWait, let me re-examine. \n\nThe regex pattern breaks down into four capture groups: everything up to the last number (including non-digits or string start), any leading zeros before that number, the number itself, and anything after. When applied to `/page%205`, it captures the `5` as the final digit sequence, with `/page%20` as the preceding content. After incrementing to 6, the result becomes `/page%206`. ` would match `2`, but that's a digit, so backtrack again. `.*` matches `/page`, and `\\D` matches `%` since it's not a digit. Group 1 captures `/page%`. Then `(0*)` matches zero zeros, `(\\d+)` greedily matches `20`, and `(.*)` matches the final `5`.\n\nWith `fullmatch`, the entire string must be consumed by the pattern. For `/page%205`, the regex `(.*\\D|^)(0*)(\\d+)(.*)` requires the first group to match either a non-digit preceded by anything or the start of the string, followed by optional zeros, then one or more digits, then anything remaining.\n\nBreaking down `/page%205`: the `.*\\D|^` part captures `/page%`, the `0*` captures nothing, `\\d+` captures `205`, and `.*` captures the empty string. This increments `205` to `206`, giving `/page%206`.\n\nNow consider `http://localhost/%3A5` where the path is `/%3A5`.\n\nThe regex would match `/%3A` (with `A` as the non-digit), zero zeros, then `5` as the number, leaving nothing after. This would increment to `/%3A6`. However, the problem mentions that percent-encoded characters with digits like `%3A` are problematic—these represent actual characters (a colon in this case) and shouldn't have their digits treated as part of the number to increment.\n\nI need to reconsider what \"corrupts\" means here. If incrementing `http://localhost/%3A5` should only change the trailing `5` to `6`, but the operation corrupts `%3A`, then the result must be something other than `/%3A6`. \"\"\"Test decrementing 1 by 2 should raise an error, not produce -1.\n\n        BUG: The code checks if val <= 0 BEFORE decrementing.\n        So if val=1 and count=2, it doesn't raise.\n        Then {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01AMDEG7USPekSrTwqbTLUgN","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01LsHiL4U8TaL61sKD3jQQrU","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/TEST_SUMMARY.md","content":"# URL Increment/Decrement Bug Regression Test\n\n## Summary\n\nThis test suite (`regression_test.py`) demonstrates three critical bugs in qutebrowser's URL increment/decrement feature, which is triggered by keyboard shortcuts that increment or decrement numeric values in URLs.\n\n## Test Results\n\n**Total Tests:** 9\n- **Failed:** 4 (demonstrating the bugs)\n- **Passed:** 5 (test cases that don't fully trigger the specific bug pathways)\n\n## Bugs Demonstrated\n\n### Bug 1: Encoded Sequence Corruption\n\n**Issue:** When URLs contain percent-encoded characters that include digits (like `%3A` for colon), the increment/decrement operation corrupts these sequences.\n\n**Root Cause:** The code calls `url.path()` and similar methods which return **decoded** strings. For example:\n- Input URL: `http://localhost/%3A5`\n- Decoded path returned: `/:5`\n- After incrementing the `5`: `/:6`\n- Result: The `%3A` encoding is lost, becoming a literal `:` in the path\n\n**Test Cases:**\n1. `test_encoded_colon_with_trailing_number` - FAILS\n   - Expected: `http://localhost/%3A6`\n   - Got: `http://localhost/:6`\n\n2. `test_encoded_special_chars_preserved` - FAILS\n   - Example: `http://example.com/file%2Fname7` → Expected: `file%2Fname8`, Got: `file/name8`\n   - The `%2F` (encoded forward slash) is decoded to `/`, corrupting the intended path structure\n\n### Bug 2: Negative Value Handling\n\n**Issue:** Decrementing a number by an amount larger than the number itself produces negative values instead of raising an error.\n\n**Root Cause:** The validation at line 538 of the original code checks:\n```python\nif val <= 0:\n    raise IncDecError(\"Can't decrement {}!\".format(val), url)\nval -= count\n```\n\nThis only prevents decrementing when the CURRENT value is 0 or negative. It doesn't prevent the RESULT from being negative. For example:\n- Current value: 1\n- Decrement by: 2\n- Check passes (1 > 0)\n- Result: 1 - 2 = -1 ✗ (Should have failed)\n\n**Test Cases:**\n1. `test_decrement_one_by_two` - FAILS\n   - Input: `http://example.com/page_1`\n   - Decrement by 2\n   - Expected: IncDecError\n   - Got: `http://example.com/page_-1`\n\n2. `test_decrement_five_by_ten` - FAILS\n   - Input: `http://example.com/test_5`\n   - Decrement by 10\n   - Expected: IncDecError\n   - Got: `http://example.com/test_-5`\n\n### Bug 3: URL-Encoded Data Loss\n\n**Issue:** URL-encoded special characters are decoded during the operation and not properly preserved when the URL is reconstructed.\n\n**Root Cause:** The implementation uses:\n- `url.path()` which returns a decoded string\n- `url.query()` which returns a decoded string\n- `url.fragment()` which returns a decoded string\n\nThese decoded strings lose the original encoding information. When setting them back using `url.setPath()`, etc., the encoding is done based on the decoded value, not the original.\n\n**Test Cases:**\n1. `test_encoded_space_with_number` - PASSES\n   - This test happens to work because spaces are re-encoded consistently\n\n2. `test_query_string_encoding_preserved` - It doesn't prevent the RESULT from being negative. For example:\n- Current value: 1\n- Decrement by: 2\n- Check passes (1 > 0)\n- Result: 1 - 2 = -1 ✗ (Should have failed)\n\n**Test Cases:**\n1. `test_decrement_one_by_two` - FAILS\n   - Input: `http://example.com/page_1`\n   - Decrement by 2\n   - Expected: IncDecError\n   - Got: `http://example.com/page_-1`\n\n2. `test_decrement_five_by_ten` - FAILS\n   - Input: `http://example.com/test_5`\n   - Decrement by 10\n   - Expected: IncDecError\n   - Got: `http://example.com/test_-5`\n\n### Bug 3: URL-Encoded Data Loss\n\n**Issue:** URL-encoded special characters are decoded during the operation and not properly preserved when the URL is reconstructed.\n\n**Root Cause:** The implementation uses:\n- `url.path()` which returns a decoded string\n- `url.query()` which returns a decoded string\n- `url.fragment()` which returns a decoded string\n\nThese decoded strings lose the original encoding information. When setting them back using `url.setPath()`, etc., the encoding is done based on the decoded value, not the original.\n\n**Test Cases:**\n1. `test_encoded_space_with_number` - PASSES\n   - This test happens to work because spaces are re-encoded consistently\n\n2. `test_query_string_encoding_preserved` -
